mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Arabian Peninsula</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Arabia&amp;redirect=no" title="Arabia">Arabia</a>)</span></div>\n<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Arabia" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Arabia_(disambiguation)" title="Arabia (disambiguation)">Arabia (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><caption>Arabian peninsula (Arabia)</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" symbols</a>.</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Arabian peninsula</b>, simplified <b>Arabia</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/e&#618;/: \'a\' in \'face\'">e&#618;</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span dir="rtl" lang="ar">&#1588;&#1616;&#1576;&#1618;&#1607;&#1615; &#1575;&#1604;&#1618;&#1580;&#1614;&#1586;&#1616;&#1610;&#1585;&#1614;&#1577;&#1616; &#1575;&#1604;&#1618;&#1593;&#1614;&#1585;&#1614;&#1576;&#1616;&#1610;&#1614;&#1617;&#1577;</span>&#8206; <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="American Library Association &#8211; Library of Congress transliteration">shibhu l-jaz&#299;rati l-&#703;arabiyyah</i></i>, \'Arabian island\' or <span dir="rtl" lang="ar" title="Arabic language text">&#1580;&#1614;&#1586;&#1616;&#1610;&#1585;&#1614;&#1577;&#1615; &#1575;&#1604;&#1618;&#1593;&#1614;&#1585;&#1614;&#1576;</span> <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="American Library Association &#8211; Library of Congress transliteration">jaz&#299;ratu l-&#703;arab</i></i>, \'Island of the Arabs\'),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> of <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a> situated northeast of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabian_plate" title="Arabian plate">Arabian plate</a>. From a geographical perspective, it is considered a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">subcontinent</a> of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p><p>It is the largest peninsula in the world, at 3,237,500&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,250,000&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The peninsula consists of the countries <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The peninsula formed as a result of the rifting of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> between 56 and 23 million years ago, and is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> to the west and southwest, the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> to the northeast, the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> to the north and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> to the southeast. The peninsula plays a critical <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">geopolitical</a> role in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a> due to its vast reserves of <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>.\n</p><p>Before the modern era, it was divided into four distinct regions: <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tihamah" title="Tihamah">Tihamah</a>), <a href="/wiki/Najd" title="Najd">Najd</a> (<a href="/wiki/Al-Yamama" title="Al-Yamama">Al-Yamama</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Arabia" title="Southern Arabia">Southern Arabia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hadhramaut" title="Hadhramaut">Hadhramaut</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Arabia" title="Eastern Arabia">Eastern Arabia</a>. Hejaz and Najd make up most of Saudi Arabia. Southern Arabia consists of <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> and some parts of Saudi Arabia (<a href="/wiki/Najran_Region" title="Najran Region">Najran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jizan_Region" title="Jizan Region">Jizan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asir" title="Asir">Asir</a>) and Oman (<a href="/wiki/Dhofar_Governorate" title="Dhofar Governorate">Dhofar</a>). Eastern Arabia consists of the entire coastal strip of the Persian Gulf.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arabian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Geography of Saudi Arabia">Geography of Saudi Arabia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1529" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg/220px-Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg/330px-Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg/440px-Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Two-point-equidistant-asia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Africa, Arabian subcontinent (Asia), and Eurasia</div></div></div>\n<p>The Arabian Peninsula is located in the continent of Asia and bounded by (clockwise) the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> on the northeast, the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Hormuz" title="Strait of Hormuz">Strait of Hormuz</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Oman" title="Gulf of Oman">Gulf of Oman</a> on the east, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> on the southeast and south, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Aden" title="Gulf of Aden">Gulf of Aden</a> on the south, the <a href="/wiki/Bab-el-Mandeb" title="Bab-el-Mandeb">Bab-el-Mandeb</a> strait on the southwest and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a>, which is located on the southwest and west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica_Arabia_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica_Arabia-11">[11]</a></sup> The northern portion of the peninsula merges with the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Desert" title="Syrian Desert">Syrian Desert</a> with no clear border line, although the northern boundary of the peninsula is generally considered to be the northern borders of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica_Arabia_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica_Arabia-11">[11]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The most prominent feature of the peninsula is <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>, but in the southwest there are mountain ranges, which receive greater rainfall than the rest of the peninsula. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harrat_ash_Shaam" title="Harrat ash Shaam">Harrat ash Shaam</a> is a large volcanic field that extends from the northwestern Arabia into <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> and southern <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_boundaries">Political boundaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arabian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Political boundaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arabian_peninsula_definition.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="196" data-file-width="250" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Arabian_peninsula_definition.PNG/220px-Arabian_peninsula_definition.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/Arabian_peninsula_definition.PNG 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arabian_peninsula_definition.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Peninsula</div></div></div>\n<p>The peninsula\'s constituent countries are (clockwise north to south) <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> (UAE) on the east, <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a> on the southeast, <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a> on the south and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> at the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica_Arabia_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica_Arabia-11">[11]</a></sup> The island nation of <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> lies off the east coast of the peninsula.\n</p><p>Six countries (Saudi Arabia, Kuwait, Bahrain, Qatar, United Arab Emirates and Oman) form the Gulf Cooperation Council (GCC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="520" decoding="async" height="279" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg/350px-Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg/525px-Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg/700px-Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Arabic_peninsula_-_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arabian Peninsula and surrounding countries</div></div></div>\n<p>The Kingdom of Saudi Arabia covers the greater part of the peninsula. The majority of the population of the peninsula live in Saudi Arabia and in Yemen. The peninsula contains the world\'s largest reserves of oil. Saudi Arabia and the UAE are economically the wealthiest in the region. <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, a small peninsula in the Persian Gulf on the larger peninsula, is home of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic-language</a> television station <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> and its English-language subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_English" title="Al Jazeera English">Al Jazeera English</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, on the border with Iraq, is an important country strategically, forming one of the main staging grounds for coalition forces mounting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Iraq" title="Invasion of Iraq">invasion of Iraq</a> in 2003.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arabian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> 2000&#8211;2014<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citypopulation.de_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-citypopulation.de-15">[15]</a></sup></small></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Though historically lightly populated, political Arabia is noted for a high population growth rate &#8211; as the result of both very strong inflows of migrant labor as well as sustained high birth rates. The population tends to be relatively young and heavily skewed gender ratio dominated by males. In many states, the number of South Asians exceeds that of the local citizenry. The four smallest states (by area), which have their entire coastlines on the Persian Gulf, exhibit the world\'s most extreme population growth, roughly tripling every 20 years. In 2014, the estimated population of the Arabian Peninsula was 77,983,936 (including expatriates).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yam_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-yam-17">[17]</a></sup> The Arabian Peninsula  is known for having one of the most uneven adult sex ratios in the world with females in some regions (especially the east) constituting only a quarter of vicenarians and tricenarians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="21-chromosome">21-chromosome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arabian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 21-chromosome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="551" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg/220px-Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg/330px-Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg/440px-Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Distribution_Haplogroup_J1_Y-DNA.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Distribution of J1 haplogroup</div></div></div>\n<p>Listed here are the <a href="/wiki/Human_Y-chromosome_DNA_haplogroup" title="Human Y-chromosome DNA haplogroup">human Y-chromosome DNA haplogroups</a> in Arabia (Yemen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Oman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Qatar,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Kuwait,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas.xyvy.info_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-atlas.xyvy.info-23">[23]</a></sup> and the United Arab Emirates) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_J-P209" title="Haplogroup J-P209">Haplogroup J</a> is the most abundant component in the Arabian peninsula, embracing more than 50% of its Y-chromosomes. Its two main subclades (<a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_J-M267" title="Haplogroup J-M267">J1-M267</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_J-M172" title="Haplogroup J-M172">J2-M172</a>), show opposite latitudinal gradients in the Middle East. J1-M267 is more abundant in the southern areas, reaching a frequency around 73% in Yemen, whereas J2-M172 is more common in the Levant.\n</p><p>J (L222.2) Accounts for the majority of (L147.1) in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>. It seems to be an exclusively <a href="/wiki/Adnan" title="Adnan">Adnani</a> marker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atlas.xyvy.info_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-atlas.xyvy.info-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Haplogroup J 54.8% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haplogroup_E_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup E (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup E</a> 17.5% R 11.6% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_T-M184" title="Haplogroup T-M184">Haplogroup T-M184</a> 5.1%\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landscape">Landscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arabian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Landscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_journey.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="499" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_journey.jpg/200px-A_journey.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_journey.jpg/300px-A_journey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/A_journey.jpg/400px-A_journey.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A caravan crossing <a href="/wiki/Ad-Dahna_Desert" title="Ad-Dahna Desert">Ad-Dahna Desert</a> in central Saudi Arabia</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ras_al_jinz_flickr01.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="632" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Ras_al_jinz_flickr01.jpg/200px-Ras_al_jinz_flickr01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Ras_al_jinz_flickr01.jpg/300px-Ras_al_jinz_flickr01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Ras_al_jinz_flickr01.jpg/400px-Ras_al_jinz_flickr01.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Ras_al-Jinz" title="Ras al-Jinz">Ras al-Jinz</a>, southeastern Arabia (Oman) also known as the \'Turtle Beach\'</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arabian_Plate_map-uni.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="604" data-file-width="562" decoding="async" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Arabian_Plate_map-uni.png/200px-Arabian_Plate_map-uni.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Arabian_Plate_map-uni.png/300px-Arabian_Plate_map-uni.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Arabian_Plate_map-uni.png/400px-Arabian_Plate_map-uni.png 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">AR-Arabian Plate, velocities with respect to Africa in millimeters per year</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Geologically, this region is perhaps more appropriately called the Arabian subcontinent because it lies on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tectonic_plate" title="Tectonic plate">tectonic plate</a> of its own, the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Plate" title="Arabian Plate">Arabian Plate</a>, which has been moving incrementally away from the rest of Africa (forming the Red Sea) and north, toward Asia, into the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a> (forming the <a href="/wiki/Zagros_Mountains" title="Zagros Mountains">Zagros Mountains</a>). The rocks exposed vary systematically across Arabia, with the oldest rocks exposed in the <a href="/wiki/Arabian-Nubian_Shield" title="Arabian-Nubian Shield">Arabian-Nubian Shield</a> near the Red Sea, overlain by earlier sediments that become younger towards the Persian Gulf. Perhaps the best-preserved <a href="/wiki/Ophiolite" title="Ophiolite">ophiolite</a> on Earth, the <a href="/wiki/Semail_Ophiolite" title="Semail Ophiolite">Semail Ophiolite</a>, lies exposed in the mountains of the UAE and northern Oman.\n</p><p>The peninsula consists of:\n</p>\n<ol><li>A central plateau, the <a href="/wiki/Najd" title="Najd">Najd</a>, with fertile valleys and pastures used for the grazing of <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">sheep</a> and other livestock</li>\n<li>A range of deserts: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nefud" title="Nefud">Nefud</a> in the north,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prothero15_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prothero15-29">[29]</a></sup> which is stony; the <a href="/wiki/Rub%27_al_Khali" title="Rub\' al Khali">Rub\' al Khali</a> or Great <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Desert" title="Arabian Desert">Arabian Desert</a> in the south, with sand estimated to extend 600&#160;ft (180&#160;m) below the surface; between them, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dahna" title="Dahna">Dahna</a></li>\n<li><a href="#Mountains">Mountains</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burrows2010_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burrows2010-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laughlin2008_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Laughlin2008-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish2007_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish2007-32">[32]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Stretches of dry or marshy coastland with coral reefs on the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> side (<a href="/wiki/Tihamah" title="Tihamah">Tihamah</a>)</li>\n<li>Oases and marshy coast-land in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Arabia" title="Eastern Arabia">Eastern Arabia</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> side, the most important of which are those of <a href="/wiki/Al_Ain" title="Al Ain">Al Ain</a> (in the UAE, on the border with Oman) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Hasa" title="Al-Hasa">Al-Hasa</a> (in Saudi Arabia), according to one author<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish2007_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish2007-32">[32]</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>Arabia has few lakes or permanent rivers. Most areas are drained by ephemeral watercourses called <a href="/wiki/Wadi" title="Wadi">wadis</a>, which are dry except during the rainy season. Plentiful ancient <a href="/wiki/Aquifer" title="Aquifer">aquifers</a> exist beneath much of the peninsula, however, and where this water surfaces, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oases" title="Oases">oases</a> form (e.g. Al-Hasa and <a href="/wiki/Qatif" title="Qatif">Qatif</a>, two of the world\'s largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oases" title="Oases">oases</a>) and permit agriculture, especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_trees" title="Palm trees">palm trees</a>, which allowed the peninsula to produce more <a href="/wiki/Date_palm" title="Date palm">dates</a> than any other region in the world. In general, the climate is extremely hot and <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">arid</a>, although there are exceptions. Higher elevations are made temperate by their altitude, and the Arabian Sea coastline can receive surprisingly cool, humid breezes in summer due to cold upwelling offshore. The peninsula has no thick forests. Desert-adapted wildlife is present throughout the region.\n</p><p>According to NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/Gravity_Recovery_and_Climate_Experiment" title="Gravity Recovery and Climate Experiment">Gravity Recovery and Climate Experiment</a> (GRACE) satellite data (2003&#8211;2013) analysed in a <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Irvine" title="University of California, Irvine">University of California, Irvine (UCI)</a>-led study published in <a href="/wiki/Water_Resources_Research" title="Water Resources Research">Water Resources Research</a> on 16 June 2015, the most over-stressed aquifer system in the world is the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Aquifer_System" title="Arabian Aquifer System">Arabian Aquifer System</a>, upon which more than 60 million people depend for water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_GRACE_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_GRACE-33">[33]</a></sup> Twenty-one of the thirty seven largest aquifers "have exceeded sustainability tipping points and are being depleted" and thirteen of them are "considered significantly distressed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA_GRACE_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-NASA_GRACE-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A plateau more than 2,500 feet (760&#160;m) high extends across much of the Arabian Peninsula. The plateau slopes eastwards from the massive, rifted escarpment along the coast of the Red Sea, to the shallow waters of the Persian Gulf. The interior is characterised by <i>cuestas</i> and valleys, drained by a system of <i>wadis</i>. A crescent of sand and <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravel</a> deserts lies to the east.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mountains">Mountains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arabian_Peninsula&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mountains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1964" data-file-width="3152" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg/220px-Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg/330px-Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg/440px-Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jebel_Hafeet_sunrise.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jebel_Hafeet" title="Jebel Hafeet">Jebel Hafeet</a> on the border of <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a>, near the city of <a href="/wiki/Al_Ain" title="Al Ain">Al Ain</a>. It can be considered an outlier of <a href="/wiki/Al_Hajar_Mountains" title="Al Hajar Mountains">Al Hajar Mountains</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gardner_01-2004_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gardner_01-2004-34">[34]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The peninsula has mountains present in its eastern, southern and northwestern borders. Broadly, the ranges can be grouped as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Northeast: <a href="/wiki/Al_Hajar_Mountains" title="Al Hajar Mountains">The Hajar range</a>, shared by the UAE and northern Oman<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish2007_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish2007-32">[32]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Southeast: The <a href="/wiki/Dhofar_Mountains" title="Dhofar Mountains">Dhofar Mountains</a> of southern Oman,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish2007_32-3"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish2007-32">[32]</a></sup> contiguous with the eastern Yemeni <a href="/wiki/Hadhramaut_Mountains" title="Hadhramaut Mountains">Hadhramaut</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scoville1979_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scoville1979-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GhazanfarFisher2013_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-GhazanfarFisher2013-36">[36]</a></sup></li>\n<li>West: Bordering the <a href="/wiki/Tihamah" title="Tihamah">eastern coast</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Sarawat_Mountains" title="Sarawat Mountains">Sarawat</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burrows2010_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Burrows2010-30">[30]</a></sup> which can be seen to include the <a href="/wiki/Jabal_Haraz" title="Jabal Haraz">Haraz Mountains</a> of eastern Yemen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laughlin2008_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Laughlin2008-31">[31]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Asir_Mountains" title="Asir Mountains">\'Asir</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Overstreet1977_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Overstreet1977-37">[37]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hijaz_Mountains" title="Hijaz Mountains">Hijaz Mountains</a> of western Saudi Arabia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mandal1990_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mandal1990-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nasr2013_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nasr2013-39">[39]</a></sup> the latter including the <a href="/wiki/Midian_Mountains" title="Midian Mountains">Midian</a> in northwestern Saudi Arabia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scoville1979_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Scoville1979-35">[35]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Northwest: Aside from the Sarawat, the northern portion of Saudi Arabia hosts the <a href="/wiki/Shammar_Mountains" title="Shammar Mountains">Shammar Mountains</a>, which include the Aja and <a href="/wiki/Salma_Mountains" title="Salma Mountains">Salma</a> subranges<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish2007_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish2007-32">[32]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Central: The Najd hosts the <a href="/wiki/Tuwaiq" title="Tuwaiq">Tuwaiq</a> Escarpment<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scoville1979_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-Scoville1979-35">[35]</a></sup> or Tuwair range<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish2007_32-5"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish2007-32">[32]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>From the <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> southwards, the mountains show a steady increase in altitude westward as they get nearer to Yemen, and the highest peaks and ranges are all located in Yemen. The highest, <a href="/wiki/Jabal_An-Nabi_Shu%27ayb" title="Jabal An-Nabi Shu\'ayb">Jabal An-Nabi Shu\'ayb</a> of the Haraz subrange of the Sarawat range, is about 3,666&#160;m (2.278&#160;mi) high.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burrows2010_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-Burrows2010-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laughlin2008_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-Laughlin2008-31">[31]</a></sup> By comparison, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuwayr_Mountains" title="Tuwayr Mountains">Tuwayr</a>, Shammar and Dhofar generally do not exceed 1,000&#160;m (0.62&#160;mi) in height.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavendish2007_32-6"><a href="#cite_note-Cavendish2007-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>It should be noted that not all mountains in the peninsula are visibly within ranges. <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Hafeet" title="Jebel Hafeet">Jebel Hafeet</a> in particular, on the border of the UAE and Oman, measuring between 1,100 and 1,300&#160;m (3,600 and 4,300&#160;ft),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gardner_01-2004_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gardner_01-2004-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LiethMasoom2012_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-LiethMasoom2012-40">[40]</a></sup> is not within the Hajar range, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sensu_stricto" title="Sensu stricto">sensu stricto</a></i>, but may be considered an <a href="/wiki/Outlier" title="Outlier">outlier</a> of that range.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Contrasting_Landscape.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3355" data-file-width="5032" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Contrasting_Landscape.jpg/270px-Contrasting_Landscape.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Contrasting_Landscape.jpg/405px-Contrasting_Landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Contrasting_Landscape.jpg/540px-Contrasting_Landscape.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>The northeastern Hajar Mountains, shared by Oman and the UAE, as seen from the desert of <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Sharjah" title="Emirate of Sharjah">Sharjah</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155.33333333333px"><div style="width: 155.33333333333px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 153.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" southeastern Oman, where the city of <a href="/wiki/Salalah" title="Salalah">Salalah</a> is located, is a tourist destination known for its annual <i><a href="/wiki/Khareef" title="Khareef">khareef</a></i> season\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tuwaik_escarpment-15h23m15s-s.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" Tuwaiq Escarpment or Tuwayr mountainous region in the <a href="/wiki/Najd" title="Najd">Najd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riyadh_Region" title="Riyadh Region">southwest</a> of the Saudi capital city of <a href="/wiki/Riyadh" title="Riyadh">Riyadh</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<div aria-labelledby="Mountains_in_the_Arabian_Peninsula" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="padding:3px"><table
